# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

# Kubernetes Admission Webhook Processing Chain

## Your Task

Trace the admission webhook processing chain in Kubernetes. Find Go source files across kubernetes/kubernetes and kubernetes/api that implement: the generic Webhook dispatcher (in pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/), the mutating webhook dispatcher with reinvocation logic, the validating webhook dispatcher with parallel dispatch, the WebhookAccessor abstraction layer, and the MutatingWebhookConfiguration/ValidatingWebhookConfiguration API type definitions.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [

  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes admission webhook processing chain. The answer.json file documents:

## Summary

I've traced the **Kubernetes admission webhook processing chain** and documented:

### **Key Components Found:**

1. **Generic Webhook Dispatcher** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/webhook.go`)
   - Abstract admission plugin infrastructure
   - Delegates to type-specific dispatchers via the `Dispatcher` interface

2. **Mutating Webhook Dispatcher** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go`)
   - Sequential webhook invocation
   - Implements reinvocation logic when objects are modified by earlier admission plugins

3. **Mutating Webhook Reinvocation Context** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/reinvocationcontext.go`)
   - Tracks object state changes and which webhooks need reinvocation
   - Detects mutations from in-tree admission plugins

4. **Validating Webhook Dispatcher** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/dispatcher.go`)
   - Parallel goroutine-based webhook invocation for performance
   - Caches versioned attributes for reuse across parallel calls

5. **WebhookAccessor Abstraction** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/accessors.go`)
   - Common interface for both mutating and validating webhooks
   - Concrete implementations: `mutatingWebhookAccessor` and `validatingWebhookAccessor`

6. **Configuration Managers**
   - `mutatingWebhookConfigurationManager` and `validatingWebhookConfigurationManager`
   - Use informers to dynamically watch MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects

7. **API Type Definitions** (kubernetes-api

Concrete implementations are:\\n- mutatingWebhookAccessor: wraps v1.MutatingWebhook and created by NewMutatingWebhookAccessor()\\n- validatingWebhookAccessor: wraps v1.ValidatingWebhook and created by NewValidatingWebhookAccessor()\\n\\nThis abstraction allows the generic webhook processing logic to work uniformly with both webhook types.\\n\\n## Mutating Webhook Dispatcher with Reinvocation Logic\\n\\nThe mutatingDispatcher (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go) implements sequential webhook invocation with critical reinvocation logic. Iterates through webhooks sequentially, invoking each one\\n4. If the object is modified by a previous admission plugin, it determines which webhooks should be reinvoked\\n5. Stores patch information in audit annotations\\n\\nThe reinvocation mechanism uses webhookReinvokeContext (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/reinvocationcontext.go) to track:\\n- lastWebhookOutput: The object state after the last webhook invocation\\n- previouslyInvokedReinvocableWebhooks: Webhooks that have been invoked\\n- reinvokeWebhooks: Webhooks that should be reinvoked during the current reinvocation phase\\n\\nThis ensures that if in-tree admission plugins mutate the object, previously invoked webhooks that should react to those changes are called again.\\n\\n## Validating Webhook Dispatcher with Parallel Dispatch\\n\\nThe validatingDispatcher (staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/dispatcher.go) implements parallel webhook invocation for performance. When Dispatch is called, it:\\n\\n1. First determines all relevant webhooks by matching rules, namespace selectors, and object selectors sequentially\\n2. Pre-creates versioned attributes for all matched webhooks and caches them in a map\\n3. Spawns goroutines for each relevant webhook to invoke them in parallel\\n4. Uses sync.WaitGroup and error channels to coordinate parallel execution\\n5. Collects errors from all webhooks and returns early if any webhook denies the request\\n\\nThe versionedAttributeAccessor caches versioned attributes to allow efficient reuse across parallel webhook calls, avoiding redundant object conversions.\\n\\n## API Type Definitions\\n\\nThe MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration types are defined in the kubernetes-api repository:\\n- admissionregistration/v1/types.go: Contains the current stable GA API versions\\n- admissionregistration/v1beta1/types.go: Contains deprecated v1beta1 API versions\\n\\nMutatingWebhookConfiguration contains a list of MutatingWebhook objects, each specifying rules, client configuration, failure policy, namespace/object selectors, and side effects. ValidatingWebhookConfiguration similarly contains ValidatingWebhook objects with the same matching and configuration fields.\\n\\n## Processing Flow\\n\\nWhen an admission request is made:\\n1. The plugin's Admit (for mutating) or Validate (for validating) method is called\\n2. This invokes the generic Webhook's Dispatch method\\n3. Dispatch calls the dispatcher's Dispatch method\\n4. The dispatcher retrieves webhooks from the configuration manager's Source\\n5. For mutating webhooks: sequential invocation with reinvocation tracking for object changes\\n6. For validating webhooks: parallel invocation with pre-cached versioned attributes\\n7. Results are collected and the request is either admitted, rejected, or admitted with modifications (mutating only)\\n\\nThe entire system is dynamic - webhook configurations are watched by informers and changes are reflected immediately without requiring API server restart.\"\n}\n",

Collects errors from all webhooks and returns early if any webhook denies the request\\n\\nThe versionedAttributeAccessor caches versioned attributes to allow efficient reuse across parallel webhook calls, avoiding redundant object conversions.\\n\\n## API Type Definitions\\n\\nThe MutatingWebhookConfiguration and ValidatingWebhookConfiguration types are defined in the kubernetes-api repository:\\n- admissionregistration/v1/types.go: Contains the current stable GA API versions\\n- admissionregistration/v1beta1/types.go: Contains deprecated v1beta1 API versions\\n\\nMutatingWebhookConfiguration contains a list of MutatingWebhook objects, each specifying rules, client configuration, failure policy, namespace/object selectors, and side effects. ValidatingWebhookConfiguration similarly contains ValidatingWebhook objects with the same matching and configuration fields.\\n\\n## Processing Flow\\n\\nWhen an admission request is made:\\n1. The plugin's Admit (for mutating) or Validate (for validating) method is called\\n2. This invokes the generic Webhook's Dispatch method\\n3. Dispatch calls the dispatcher's Dispatch method\\n4. The dispatcher retrieves webhooks from the configuration manager's Source\\n5. For mutating webhooks: sequential invocation with reinvocation tracking for object changes\\n6. For validating webhooks: parallel invocation with pre-cached versioned attributes\\n7. Results are collected and the request is either admitted, rejected, or admitted with modifications (mutating only)\\n\\nThe entire system is dynamic - webhook configurations are watched by informers and changes are reflected immediately without requiring API server restart.\"\n}\n",
  "filePath": "/workspace/answer.json",
  "originalFile": null,
  "structuredPatch": [],
  "type": "create"
}
